Having completed for you, my children, this book, which is the last of the medical sciences with its completion, and having reached its end in its expositions and its declarations, it seemed to me to complete it for you with this treatise, which is a part of the practice, that is, of surgery, with the hand.
Since manual practice has been neglected in our region and in our time, almost entirely: until perhaps its knowledge perished, and its trace was cut off; and there remained of it only small descriptions in the books of the ancients, which were altered by hands; and error and hesitation befell them, until its intent was closed, and its power was distanced.  It seemed to me that I might revive it with the order of this treatise, according to the manner of exposition, declaration, and abbreviation; and that I might come with the forms of cautery instruments and other instruments of the work: with the addition of declaration, and with the acceleration of what is necessary.
The reason, however, why a good practitioner is not found with his skill in our time, is: because the art of medicine is long, and its author must be trained beforehand in the science of anatomy, as described by Galen, so that he knows the aids of the limbs, and their shapes, and their connections and separations, and has knowledge of the bones, and nerves, and tendons, and their number, and their courses, and the pulsating and still veins, and the places from where they exit.
And because of that, Hippocrates said that a name with a name is much, and with a work is little, and especially in the art of the hand.
We have already spoken of that at the beginning of this book.
Since he who is not knowledgeable of what we have said about anatomy is not prevented from falling into error, by which men are killed; just as I have seen many of those who are trained in this science, and boast of it without knowledge and without experience.
That is, because I saw a foolish physician cut a scrofulous boil on a woman's neck, and cut some arteries in the neck: wherefore the woman's blood flowed until she fell dead in his hands.
And I saw another physician, who presumed to extract a stone from a man who had advanced in age, and the stone was large. So he reached it, and extracted it with a piece of the bladder. Therefore the man died on the third day.
And indeed I had already been called to extract it, and I saw from the size of the stone, and the disposition of the sick man, that he would die.
And I saw another physician who was receiving a stipend from a certain Duke of our land for medicine, and a black eunuch who was with him suffered a fracture in his leg near the heel. And the physician, in his ignorance, hurried and bound the fracture over the wound with pillows and splints with strong constriction, and did not allow the wound any release.
Then he discharged him according to his own desires. Afterwards, he dismissed him after a few days, and ordered him not to loosen the bandages.  And he remained like that until his leg and foot were filled with pus, and he came to destruction.
Therefore, I was called to him, and I hurried to loosen the bandages. And tranquility followed, and he escaped his pains.
However, the corruption had already become established in the limb, and I could not restrain it.
Therefore, the corruption ceased to spread in the limb until it perished.
And I saw another physician, who pierced the cancerous abscess.  And it ulcerated after days, until its malice increased greatly with its master.
That is, when cancer is pure from melancholy humor, then it is not necessary to reach it with iron at all, unless it be in a limb that can tolerate its being entirely cut off.
And because of that, my children, it is necessary for you to know that surgical operation is divided into two divisions: namely, an operation to which health is associated, and an operation with which there is danger in many dispositions.
And I have already aroused in every place of this book, in which operation comes, in which is terror and fear.
Therefore it is necessary for you to beware of that, and to diminish it, so that fools may not find a way to speak ill of and dishonor it.
Therefore, receive the measure with care and protection, and your sick with ease and firmness, and use the better way leading by God's grace to health and praiseworthy success; and leave the terrible sicknesses of difficult healing; and remove your souls from that which makes you fear, so that hesitation may enter upon your faith and your benefit.
For it is more remaining to your glory, and more lofty in this world, and finally to your quantities.
For Galen already said in some of his admonitions. Do not treat bad illness; lest you be called bad physicians.
Now, however, I have divided this Treatise into three Chapters.
First Chapter.
Concerning the cautery with fire, and the cautery with sharp medicine, discussed and ordered from head to foot, and concerning the forms of instruments, and the iron implements of the cautery: and everything that is necessary in the operation.
Second Chapter.
Concerning incision and perforation, bloodletting and cupping, and wounds: and the extraction of arrows, and similar things: and the entire discussion, ordered by the forms of instruments.
Third Chapter.
Concerning restoration, and dislocation, and the treatment of twisting, and similar things: discussed, ordered from head to foot, and concerning the forms of instruments.
But before I recount the operation with it, it is necessary that I speak of the quality of its benefits and harms, and in what complexion it should be applied.
I say therefore, that the discussion of the quality of the cautery's benefit and harm is a lengthy and subtle discussion, requiring knowledge and a hidden secret.
Many wise men have also spoken on it, and they disagreed on it; and for me, a little from their discussions suffices, fearing a prolongation.
I say therefore, that cautery benefits universally any complexion that is with matter, and without matter; except for the two complexions which are the hot complexion without matter and the dry complexion without matter.
However, in the hot and dry complexion with matter, they disagreed. For some said that cautery is beneficial in it. And others said the opposite, namely that cautery is not suitable in an illness that arises from heat and dryness, because the nature of fire is heat, and it is inappropriate that one is healed from a hot and dry illness with heat and dryness.
And he who says the opposite stated that through cautery benefit is achieved in every hot and dry illness that occurs in human bodies, because when you compare the human body and its humors to the complexion of fire, you find the human body to be cold.
And I indeed say through his words, because by experience it has repeatedly revealed that to me.
However, it should not be applied unless one is already proven and practiced in the final exercise of the cautery chapter, and has known the diversity of human complexions and the disposition of illnesses within themselves, and their causes, and their accidents, and their duration.
However, there is no fear from the remaining complexions, and especially in cold and moist illnesses. For all physicians have agreed upon them, and have not disagreed on their benefit with cautery in them.
And know, children, that the secret of curing by cautery with fire, and its goodness over cautery with burning medicine, is that fire is simple, whose action does not reach, except the limb which is cauterized: and it does not harm another limb joined with it, except with little harm.
However, the action of burning medicine reaches that which is distant from the limbs, and perhaps causes the limb to suffer from a difficult-to-heal illness, and perhaps kills it.
However, fire, because of its subtlety and the goodness of its substance, does not do that, unless it overflows.
Now, however, that has become known to us through experiment, due to the length of service and study with the art, and our standing on the truth of things; and because of that, I excuse myself from the length of speech.
And if it were not so, because it is not permitted to this book of mine, I would reveal to you the hidden secret in fire, and the quality of its operation on bodies from its expulsion, by which it expels illnesses, demonstrated in a philosophical and demonstrative manner, to be sharpened by your minds.
And know, children, that they disagree on the time when the cautery should be applied, and they posit a better time as the vernal season.
And I say that cautery is appropriate at all times, because the harm, being accidental, is submerged in the benefit attracted by the cautery. And especially if the cautery is for pains from necessary, strong, urgent pains, which do not tolerate slowness; because it is feared from these that a greater harm will occur than the slight harm entering due to time.
And do not let it enter your minds, O children, that which the common people and foolish physicians fear, namely that the illness cured by cautery does not always return; and they posit that as a consequence, and the matter is not as they suppose; for cautery is nothing but a substitute for medicine, which alters the complexion and dries out the humidities that are the cause why the pains occur.
However, cautery excels medicine in the swiftness of its effect, and the strength of its operation, and the intensity of its control; and it is possible that the illness may return at some time according to the patient's complexion, and the location of the illness, and its strength, and what is prepared in the body from the accumulation of superfluities in it, and what reaches it in its acquisition from foods, and similar causes, unless it is an illness to which cautery is administered.
A subtle illness in a limb with few superfluities and humidities, like the toothache, because of the pain, and similar to it, it is possible that that pain will not return to it. But that happens in few cases.
But truly the common people's talk, that cautery is the last resort of medicine, is correct speech; not in the way they intend it, because they believe that there is no cure to compare with medicine, nor anything after the cautery's application.
However, the matter is the opposite of that, and the intention that cautery is medicine's last resort is not, except that when we apply methods of treatment in some illnesses and those treatments do not succeed; then, at the end of the matter, we apply cautery, and it succeeds.  Then it follows that cautery is medicine's last resort, not according to the intention understood by the common people and many unskilled physicians.
The ancients said that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron, and they did not say this except because of the equality of gold and the sublimity of its substance; and they said that the cautery site does not produce pus. But that is not absolutely so, because I have already tested it, and found that it does not do that in some bodies without others.
And cautery with it [gold] is good, and better than with iron, as they said. However, when you apply cautery with gold in fire, it is not clear to you when the heat reaches the desired intensity, because of the gold's redness; and when it rapidly cools, and if you add more heat to it, it melts in the fire and turns into thin sheets.
Therefore, the craftsman is deterred from using it [gold cautery]; and for that reason cautery with iron is faster and closer to us, by virtue of its suitability for the operation.
And I have indeed already arranged this chapter on cautery according to its chapters; and I have arranged them from head to foot, so that they will help the one seeking what he wants from it.
Chapter Two.
This cauterization is beneficial for controlling the excess of moisture and cold upon the brain; these two are the causes of headaches, and the excessive flow of humors from the head to the eyes and ears, and of excessive sleep, and toothache, and sore throat; and universally all sickness which arises from cold, such as paralysis, and headaches, epilepsy, and apoplexies, and similar illnesses.
The method of cauterization is that you should first instruct the sick person to be purged with a cleansing solution, cleaning the head for three or four nights, according to the strength of the sick person, and their age, and their habits.
Then instruct them to shave their head with a razor. Then make him sit between your hands squarely, so that he has already placed his hands upon his chest.
Then place the root of your palm upon the root of his nose between his eyes. Wherever therefore your middle finger reaches, mark that spot with the cautery.
Then apply the olive-shaped cautery to it: which has this shape.
Then place it upon the spot marked with the cautery, descending, so that your hand may gradually constrict it, and you shall turn it. Then lift your hand quickly, and look at the spot.
If you see now uncovered from the bone a quantity of alkiel, or a quantity of zeuherbi, then lift your hand. And if not, repeat the application of your hand with the iron itself, or with another from the same if it cools: until the bones which I have told you appear.
Then take some salt, and dissolve it in water, and soak the cloth in it, and place it over the spot: and leave it for three days.
Then place the soaked cloth in butter over it, and leave it over the spot until the scab of fire is destroyed. Then treat it with tetrapharmacon ointment, until it is healed.
They have said that the more a wound remains open, the more pus it emits: wherefore it is better and more helpful.
And some of them said that the skin should be cauterized down to the bone: and the cautery should be held until something the thickness of bone is burned.
Then that which is burned from the bone should be shaved off, then treated.
And others say that it is necessary to reach the utmost with the cautery, until it presses an impression in the bone, so that the bone falls, which is done like a kirate shape: or an instrument which women place on a small alphabetic infusion: and they suppose that vapors of the head are exhaled from this place, and the wound should be left open for a long time.
Then it should be treated until it is consolidated.
However, these two types of cautery do not seem to me to be suitable except in certain individuals, according to the way of fear.
And to leave it, in my opinion, is better with the health of the individual.
For the head is weakened by the disruption of its natural continuity, as we have testified in other limbs, and especially when the head of the infirm is naturally weak; and indeed the first type of cautery is more healthful and better in my opinion, and I use it; therefore operate with it for health.
Chapter III.
When chronic pain occurs in the entire head, and it is prolonged in the infirm person, and he/she uses leeches, and cupping, and head-cleansers, and oils, and plasters. And especially if it has already been cauterized with the single cautery, which we have described, and none of those things helps it, then consider. For if the head of the sick person is of strong natural constitution, and is not weak, and finds intense cold, then cauterize with another cautery slightly beneath the first. Then cauterize it above every horn of its head with a cautery, so that the skin is not pierced, and a quantity is uncovered from the bone, as we have described. And cauterize it with a single cautery on the back of its head, in the place called the vein: and it is the place where a cupping glass is placed: and raise your cautery here, and do not uncover the bone. For the sick person finds, because of that, a severe pain, and different from the pain of the other cauterizations of all the head.
And I shall say that this cautery is in its proper place: and it should be the cautery with which the horns of the head are cauterized, and the back of his head with a finer cautery, with which the middle of the head is cauterized.
Chapter IV.
When pain and throbbing occur in a part of the head, or the pain extends to the eye, and the head is cleansed with purifying medicines, and the rest of the treatment, which I described in the divisions of illnesses, is administered, and it does not benefit the whole condition: then cauterization is appropriate in it according to two methods: either cauterization with a burning, sharp medicine, or with iron.
The cautery with a burning, sharp medicine is as follows: take one clove of garlic, and peel it, and cut off its ends from both sides. Then, incise the painful area with a wide phlebotom knife, until a space is made under the skin where the clove can be placed.
Then introduce it into the space under the skin, until it is hidden; then bind over it with a bandage of suitable constriction, and leave it for fifteen hours. Then loosen it, and remove the garlic, and let the wound rest for two or three days. Afterwards, apply a poultice soaked in butter to it until the area produces pus. Then treat it with ointment until it heals.
And if you wish, do it with certain burning medicines, which I wrote in the twelfth treatise, on Burning Medicines.
The cauterization of it with iron, is according to this method. The cauterium of fire, whose form is this.
And it is called a Clavil, because the shape of its head is like the shape of a nail, in which there is some curvature, and in its middle there is a small prominence.
Then place it upon the area, and hold your hand; and you revolve the iron slowly with speed; and let the quantity that is burned be from the thickness of the skin, like half of it. And raise your hand, so that the artery, which is below, is not burned, and a flow of blood occurs.
Then soak the cloth in salt water, and place it over the area, and leave it for three days; then place the cloth with butter; afterwards treat with ointment until it heals.
And if you wish, cauterize this hemicrania with the second cautery's knife-like extremity. And beware of cutting the artery in this hemicrania, not properly ancient.
On the method of cauterizing in ancient hemicrania.
When treating hemicrania, along with what we have said from the preceding treatment, and what we have said in the divisions of diseases, and if treatment does not help: and if you see from the illness that what we have said from the first cautery with medicine, or with cautery with fire, is not sufficient, then it is necessary to heat the knife-like cautery until it turns white, after having marked the site of pain with a line, whose length is half a finger, or approximately that: and place your hand in turn, and press it until you cut the artery, and reach the bone.
However, it is necessary for you to beware of the continuation of the jaw, which moves during mastication, lest the side or the nerve that moves it be burned, whence spasm may result.
And be on guard, and careful of the flow of blood from the severed artery. For in its severing lies danger, and especially for him who does not know what he is doing, and is not studious nor experienced: and he abandons the operation with that in the first place.
And I will come with a reminder of the regimen for blood flow arising from an artery according to its manner and in the place of this book.
If you see from the illness that this cautery is not sufficient for him, and you see the body of the sick person tolerating a cautery in the middle of the head, as we have narrated, treat the wound until it heals.
And if you wish, administer the cautery, which we have said in the chapter on the extraction of the artery with a cautery having two knives. For cauterization is better than this and more beneficial.
Concerning the method of cauterization in earache.
When pain in the ear occurs from cold, and is treated with remedies, and with the remaining treatment that we have mentioned in the division, and the pain does not subside, then use fire with the cautery: and it is that which is called the Point, whose shape is this.
Then, after igniting it, apply the points in a circular motion around the entire ear, as it revolves, or in a circular motion around each ear, if the pain is in both at the same time. And move the cautery slightly away from the base of the ear, after you have marked the areas with the marking ink; and let the quantity of the cautery be ten points on each ear, and like that.
Then treat the areas until they are healed.
Concerning the method of cauterization in a twisting motion.
Chapter VII.
The twisting that is cured with cauterization is only from the types that occur from phlegm, according to what we said in the divisions of illnesses.
And avoid cauterization of the type that occurs from dryness and nerve spasm.
When you treat this type of twisting with leeches, and head-cleansings, and gargles, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize the afflicted with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and a second a little lower from its temporal location, and a third at the juncture of the two lips.
And place your cautery opposite the afflicted part. Because softening does not occur unless in the part that appears healthy.
And the form of cauterization is that you cauterize it with the cautery directly at the extremity of the upper ear, below the horn of the head a little; and another in the temporal region, whose length should be according to the length of a thumb. And hold your hand with the cautery until a quantity equal to half the thickness of the skin is burned.
And this is the form of the cautery, and it is a type of knife, whose form has been mentioned before; however, it is not less sharp by a little, as you see; and it is necessary for the knife to be somewhat free of superfluous thickness.
Then treat the places, with what has gone before, until they are healed.
Concerning the method of cauterization in old apoplexy.
When apoplexy becomes old, and you have treated it with what we said, and your treatment does not help, and the sick person does not have a fever, then cauterize him with four cauteries on each horn of his head, and with a cautery in the middle of the head, as we said, and with a cautery on the back of the head, according to what has gone before; and the method of the cautery shall be according to what has gone before.
Also, he is cauterized with a cautery on the mouth of the stomach; and this is more of a last resort.
Then, let him be treated with what has gone before.
Chapter IX.
It is necessary that in the drink, first be given to the sick large hyerae and pills that cleanse the brain.
Then shave the entire head of the sick person, and place on his occiput a plaster of mustard described in the treatise on plasters: and place it several times.
For that is the method of cautery, and do it according to the same order that I stated there.
If therefore he is cured by it, it is good. If not, then make three cauteries on the back part of his head, which shall descend from the upper part of the head down to the lower part of the eye: and place between each cautery the thickness of a finger.
Then treat the cautery, with what preceded it.
If however you wish an addition, and the sick person is unable to tolerate it, then make a cautery in the middle. If you wish an addition, then cauterize him above the two horns.
Then treat him until he is healed; and let the cautery be olive-shaped, according to the form that has been described.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in paralysis and softening.
Chapter X.
It is necessary to proceed in cleansing the head with hyeres, and with that which we have said.
Then shave the patient's head; afterwards cauterize it with a cautery in the middle of the head, and with a cautery on each horn of the head, and with a cautery on its posterior, and with three on the vertebrae of the neck.
If, however, in the sickness there is a need for the softening of the body by many cauteries, and the patient is unable to tolerate them, and the illness is severe, then cauterize him with four cauteries on the vertebrae of the back, and the last with a cautery until most of his skin is burnt, and lift your hand. Then treat him until he is healed; and thus the cautery is applied.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in Epilepsy.
An epileptic is not cauterized, unless that whose epilepsy is from phlegm.
Therefore, it is necessary that you first cleanse his brain with leeches, and with the rest of the treatment which we have mentioned in the division: when the sick person is strong, or is tolerant in accepting medicines.
However, if it is a child who does not tolerate medicines, then a gargle and chewing motions that cleanse the brain are administered, many days beforehand with an improvement in food.
Then shave his head, afterwards cauterize him with one cautery in the middle of the head, according to what preceded in the manner, and with another cautery on his occiput, and with a cautery on each horn of his head. If, however, the patient is strong and tolerant, then cauterize him with the cauteries that I have described in the case of paralysis, and for the softening of the body upon the vertebrae of the neck and vertebrae of the back: and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to the manner which has preceded.
If however the patient is a child, then apply a fine cautery, according to this method.
Concerning the method of cauterization in Melancholy.
When the cause of melancholy is corrupted humours and thick phlegm, then cauterize him with the cauteries that we have mentioned in the case of paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is a superfluity sloping towards melancholy, and the patient's body is moist, then give him a drink that will purify his brain, according to what was said previously in the division. Then shave the patient's head, and afterwards make a well-made linen roll, like a circle.
Then place it in the middle of the head, and let the patient sit upright, held fast on all sides.
Then apply the liniment. And it is better made from old sheep's butter. And heat it over a fire with a moderate heat, which a finger can tolerate when placed within it. Then apply it to the middle of his head in a circular motion, and leave it until it cools.
Do this to the sick person once a week, with the rest of his good regimen, until he is healed.
Or if you wish, cauterize it by making many small points on it, beyond which you should hold the cautery: indeed, let it be by smelling.
For this type of cautery moistens the brain with quality.
Then place on it a poultice soaked in butter, or chicken fat.
Concerning the method of cauterization in descending water to the eye.
Chapter XIII.
When you are shown the beginning of water in the eye, by the signs that I have mentioned in the division, then begin and let the infirm drink, with that which will cleanse his head.
And keep him from all dampness, and have him sit in a bath, fasting for several days.
Then order him to shave his head, and cauterize him in the middle of his head. Then cauterize him on the two temples with two cauteries, if the descent of water is beginning in both eyes simultaneously; or on one side, if the beginning is in one eye; and cut with the cautery all the veins and arteries that are under the skin; and let the cauteries be of the same length as the width of the temples; and beware of the flow of blood.
If you see something from it, then remove it immediately with whatever medicine is possible; and I will come with the knowledge that is in extracting arteries, and cutting them, and caution concerning the flow of blood.
And sometimes he is cauterized on the neck, beneath the two bones, with two cauteries finally produced.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in ancient lachrymal passages.
When the tears of the eyes are old, persistent; and they are above the veins and arteries that are in the obvious exterior of the head, it is verified that it is from cold, phlegmatic superfluities; then cauterize with the same cautery that I have narrated in the beginning of descending water, a cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauteries above the two temples, and two cauteries on the neck beneath the two bones. And if it needs an addition, then cauterize it on every side of the eye's cavity, above the end of the eyebrow with a small cautery.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in a foul odor of the nose.
When you treat it, with what we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help; then hurry, and give in a drink to the sick person cochlias three nights; afterwards shave his head, and cauterize it with a middle cautery, with an olive cautery. Then cauterize it with a clavicle cautery, two cauteries, above the two eyebrows beneath the hair a little.
And guard against the artery, lest you strike it.
And this is the form of the Clavulus cautery.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in softening the eyelid.
When the eyelid of the eye is softened by illness or moisture, then cauterize the eyelid with one cautery, using this lunate cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize it above the two eyebrows slightly with two cauteries on every side, and let them be distant from the two temples; and let the length of each cautery be according to the length of the eyebrow; and do not place your hand with the cautery to the end, but according to the amount that the third eyelid is burned.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the eyelid when the hairs are inverted, pricking the eye.
The cautery in it is according to two methods: either cautery with fire, or cautery with a burning medicine.
In cautery with fire, beforehand command the infirm person to remove his hairs, if he is of those who cleanse them, until they are extended and made equal. If however they prick him at their origin: then bind his eyes with a bandage, so that they do not move, until they are born.
When therefore they are born and made equal, then place the head of the infirm person in your bosom; then mark above the eyelid of his eyes with encaustic, a sign that is according to the shape of a myrtle leaf; and let the beginning of the sign be near the hairs.
Then place a cloth soaked in egg white, or in psyllium mucilage, upon the eye.
Then apply a cautery, whose shape is this.
Then cauterize over the shape you marked, gradually in many stages, until the surface of the skin, which is like the shape of a myrtle leaf, is entirely burnt away.
And the sign of the success of your work is: that if you see the eyelid of the eye already contracting, and the hairs rising at the puncture of the eye.
Therefore raise your hand then, and leave it for three days.
Then place upon it a cloth with butter, until the eschar is removed. Then treat it with ointment until it heals.
If any hair returns after an hour, and the eyelid softens: then again cauterize that place, as you did at first.
If, however, the hairs are in the lower part, then cauterize it until it is raised to its natural place and is even so that the hairs do not prick the eye.
You should instruct the sick person to let the hairs go, until they are lengthened and made even. Make a shape of a myrtle leaf from paper or cloth.
Then take one ounce, or almost that amount, of known soap and of unsoaked lime; then grind them together well, and do it quickly so that it does not get cold. Then spread some of it over the paper you made in the shape of a myrtle leaf, and put it over the eyelid of one or two eyes. And place under the eye a cloth soaked in egg white; and let the head of the sick person be in your bosom.
And place your index finger on the medicine, and press it for a short time. And you should move it whenever the sick person feels the medicine's biting, because its biting is like fire.
While therefore this biting which he finds persists, then leave the medicine, and move it with your finger. When therefore the biting ceases, then remove the medicine, and wash the eye with water.
And then consider, if you see the eyelid raised, as it is raised by contraction with fire, or with incision, it is well; and if not, then repeat the medicine on the area, where the medicine does not penetrate and does not darken, until your operation is equal to, and the eye is contracted.
Then place on it Cuta with butter, until the skin of the burn is eradicated. Then treat it with diaphinicon ointment, or another, until it is healed.
And it is necessary for you during the operation to observe the utmost care, so that nothing of the medicine falls into the eye.
If the eyelid softens after days, and some hair struggles into the eye, then repeat the medicine on the area that softens from the eyelid properly, as you did at first. Then treat it until it is healed.
And this is the form of the myrtle leaf.
And know that the eyes of men differ in size and smallness. Therefore, according to that, let your consideration be: and the path of righteousness is not hidden from him who has a diligent study of this art.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in a tear duct fistula.
When you treat a fistula, in accordance with what we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you cauterize it according to this method.
Tell the sick person to place their head in your lap, and let the attendant hold their head in their hands in such a way that it does not move or tremble with their head.
Then place a cotton swab soaked in egg white, or in psyllium mucilage, over their eye; then apply the cautery, whose shape is this.
Let it be concave, like the shape of a vulture's wing feather from one end, with which the cautery is made; and if you wish to be penetrating to the other end, and if you wish to be held upward like this.
However, this concave shape is better for your work.
Then express the fistula, if it is open, and extract the pus from it, and dry it; and if it is not open, then open it, and extract its pus.
Then place the cautery, which is made very hot, upon it.
And hold your hand with the cautery for a short time near the cautery, from the eye to the side of the nose, so that your hand does not stray or disturb the sick person; and you shall place the cautery on the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
If therefore you reach the opening of your cautery at the start, it will be well. And if not, then repeat the cautery once or twice, if you need it; and leave it for three days.
Then place a compress with butter, and treat it with a drying ointment, until it is healed.
If however forty days have passed, and it is not healed, then place on it a sharp, corrosive medicine, until the opening is revealed; and scrape it according to what is stated in its chapter.
And there is another method of cauterizing a fistula, which some of the first [practitioners] said. Aim at the location of the fistula and cut it open; then place in the opening a thin camahan, that is, a thin cannula, whose shape is this. And pour into it a drachm of liquefied lead, and hold your hand with a good retaining cannula, and let the patient not move at all, so that the liquefied lead does not run, or reach his eye.
And it is necessary that you place on the patient's eye a poultice soaked in egg white, or in water.
For lead burns the area of the fistula, and heals it with a remarkable cure.
If the fistula is healed by what we have said about cautery and treatment, it is good. And if not, then it is necessary to administer a nasal opening, and to reduce the fistula to the course of the nose, according to where it will come to its proper place.
Concerning the method of cauterization in lip fissures.
Often fissures occur in the lip, called hairs, and especially in the lips of children.
Therefore, when you treat these fissures, using what we have said in the division of diseases, and if the treatment is not effective, then cauterize with a small, knife-like cautery, according to this form.
And its concavity should be according to the sharpness of the knife.
Then place it [the cautery] ignited quickly on the fissures themselves, until the cautery reaches the depth of the fissures.
Then treat it with a cauterant, until it heals.
Concerning the method of cauterization in a fistula of the mouth.
When an abscess occurs at the root of the gum, or in the palate, or in the roots of the teeth; then it produces pus, and bursts; afterwards it becomes chronic, and pus runs, and a fistula forms; then you treat it, and treatment does not help it, then it is necessary that you cauterize the wound with a cautery according to the size that it occupies in the fistula. Then introduce the heated cautery into the opening of the fistula, and hold your hand until the heated iron reaches its depth and its end; do this once or twice.
Then treat it afterwards, with that which we said about treatment until it is healed.
If therefore the pus is cut away, and it heals, it will be good. And if not, then it is necessary to uncover the place, and remove the corrupted bone according to what comes upon its head.
Concerning the method of cauterizing softened gums and teeth.
When the gum softens due to moisture, and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines, and it does not help: then place the head of the sick person in your lap.
Then take a cautery, whose shape will follow, so that you place the cannula on the tooth; and quickly insert the heated cautery into it; and hold your hand for a short time, until the sick person feels the heat of the fire already reaching the root of the tooth.
And raise your hand; then repeat the cautery several times, as desired.
Then let the sick person fill their mouth with salt water, and hold it for an hour, and spit it out.
For the moving tooth is strengthened, and the softened gum is tightened, and the corrupted moisture is dried.
Concerning the method of cauterizing dental pain.
When toothache is due to cold, or there is cold or a worm in it, and treatment with medicines does not help, then the cautery is applied to it in two ways: either cautery with butter, or cautery with fire.
However, its cautery with butter is to take milk butter and boil it in an iron spoon, or in a vessel. Then take a cotton swab and wrap it around the tip of the probe. Then immerse it in the boiled butter, and quickly place it on the aching tooth, and hold it until it cools; then repeat it several times, until the power of fire reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, immerse wool or cotton in cold butter, and place it on the aching tooth, and place hot iron on it until fire reaches the deep cavity of the tooth.
Its cauterization with fire is to aim at a brass tube, or an iron tube. And let there be something of its thickness, so that the sharpness of the fire does not reach the sick person's mouth.
Then take the cautery, whose shape will come, and place it on that tooth, and hold your hand until the cautery cools.
Do it several times, for the pain will be removed, either on that same day, or on another day.
And it is necessary that, in the application of that cautery, the sick person should fill his mouth with good butter, and hold it for an hour; then spit it out.
And this is the shape of the cautery.
Cauterize with whichever extremity of force is possible: and this is the shape of the cannula.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in strophulus.
When strophulus are caused by phlegm and by cold humors, and are not yielding to digestion by medicines, and the force of digestion of them is slow, then with a concave cautery, whose form is this, cauterize with fire.
Having two open ends, so that smoke may issue forth at one end of the cautery, and place it heated upon the abscess once, and a second time, if that is insufficient, until it reaches the depth of the abscess.
If the abscess is small, then place the cautery according to the size of the abscess.
Then leave it for three days, and place upon it a poultice infused in butter, until that which the fire burned away is removed.
Then treat it with tooth ointment, until the form of the cannula is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterization for hoarseness of voice and constriction of breathing.
When humidities overcome the lung's passages, and especially when it is with a cold temperament, then it is necessary that the infirm person be evacuated primarily with dissolving medicines.
Then cauterize it in the nocrati near the root of the throat in the depressed place: and beware, lest you reach the throat with the cautery, nor the skin, unless something of it.
Then cauterize it with another cautery at the junction of the neck at the last vertebra thereof, and let the cautery be narrow in accordance with the manner that preceded.
Then treat it with what preceded, until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterization in diseases of the lungs and cough.
When cough and lung disease are from cold humors, and the sick person does not have a fever, nor consumption, and the illness is old, then cauterize him with two cauteries above the fork in depressed, smooth, empty places. And with another cautery in the middle of the chest between the two breasts: and let the cautery be of a tube according to the form that preceded.
And if you wish your cauterization to be by puncturing with a cautery, called *Punctum*, whose form preceded in the puncturing of the pain of the ears: and let the punctures be from thirty punctures to as if another.
Then treat him with what preceded, until he is healed.
And now let the cautery have three branches: according to this form. Therefore, the cauterization is alleviated when you do it with three cauteries at once.
Chapter XXVII.
When the head of the humerus is dislocated due to moisture, and does not return to its proper place after the dislocation, until it is accustomed to returning, then it is dislocated by a small movement, as we have already testified, then you must reduce the dislocation first. Then the sick person should be laid on their back, or on their healthy side. Then lift the skin that is on the inner Titillico upwards with your left hand, and if the joint is dislocated inward.
Then, having a cautery with two prongs. Whose form is this.
Then cauterize the skin until it penetrates it to the other side, and the figure of the cauterization will come with four cauteries.
And sometimes cauterization is done with a cautery having three prongs, why the figure of cauterization then is of six cauteries: and the prongs are according to the thinness of the thread.
And this is the form of the cautery having three prongs.
And sometimes one is added to this method, why there are eight cauteries.
Then place on the cautery, crushed leeks with salt. Then make the infirm adhere to tranquility, so that the limb does not move at any time, until it is strengthened.
And if the dislocation is upwards, and rarely does that happen, then cauterize it above the shoulder with a clavicle cautery, or with many cauteries by puncturing.
For the joint is strengthened, and moisture is removed: and the infirm is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the stomach.
When there are cold and many moistures in the stomach, until they draw it from its complextion, and the phlegms multiply in it, and persistent modes of treatment do not help, then it is necessary that the sick person lie on his back, and extend his legs, and his hands. Then cauterize with three cauteries, one cautery under the spoon-shaped part of the breast to the size of one finger with a claviform cautery, and two cauteries lower down at the two sides of one cautery, until a triangular shape of cauteries is formed. And lengthen them apart so that they do not join, when they will produce pus.
And the depth of the cautery be the size of two-thirds the thickness of the skin.
And let the shape of the cauteries be according to this form without addition; and if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form, and let the cautery by which this is done be one according to the form of a circle, according to this form.
And the stomach is cauterized by puncturing it with that which is terrified by this cautery; and it is that you mark upon the stomach a point according to the quantity that you wish with encaustic; then cauterize it with the cautery of the point; then treat it with the treatment that preceded until it is healed.
Of the method of cauterizing a cold liver.
When in the liver pain occurs from cold and moisture, or from thick wind, until it emerges from its natural complexion by a superfluity's departure, and the sick person is treated with what we have said, and it does not benefit him: then it is necessary that the sick person be laid supine upon their neck, and mark with encaustic three cauteries according to this figure, and this same quantity on the lower liver from the hypochondria, where the man's elbow reaches: and let the space between each cautery be according to the thickness of a finger; and let the cautery be according to the length of the body straight; and do not press your hand with the cautery much.
And let the quantity of that which is burned be, from the thickness of the skin, the quantity of its half, not added: and let the sick person be standing on their feet.
If however he is not standing, then let him be lying, having already extended his legs, and raised his arms.
This is the form of the cautery.
And it is possible for you, to cauterize these cauteries with a knife cautery, when you have subtlety and prudence in the art.
And guard yourself so that you do not proceed too far in the cauterization, and the thickness of the entire skin is burned, for then the whole body is burned, and it reaches the intestines: for the skin there is thin, therefore know that.
On the method of cauterizing abscesses of the liver.
When an exit occurs, and you wish to know if that abscess is in the flesh of the liver, or in its tunic: then if it is in the flesh of the liver, the sick person is afflicted with pain and heaviness without sharpness; and if it is in the tunic of the liver, there is intense sharpness with the pain: and you see already that the treatment has fatigued his physicians.
Therefore, the sick person must lie on their back. Then, mark the location of the abscess with ink; then apply a cautery heated like a ray. And this is its form. And cauterize with it a single cautery, until the entire skin is burned and reaches the pus, until all the pus exits; then treat it with the treatment for exits until it is healed.
And it is not appropriate for one to use this type of cautery, unless their study in the art of medicine is prolonged, and through whose hands these illnesses have met with experience several times; for only then may one dare to undertake such an operation.
But truly, to leave it be, is better for me.
Concerning the method of cauterization in Pleuritis.
The ancients said that cautery with the roots of aristolochia, for cold pleurisy, according to this method. And it is, that you receive from the dry long roots of aristolochia, one root longer than the others found, and let it be like the thickness of a finger. Then immerse it in oil; and ignite it in fire. Then cauterize with one cautery in that which is between the continuation of the fork with the neck, and with two small cauteries a little sloping downward to the part which is under the beard.
And with two cauteries also in that which is between the fifth and sixth rib, sloping slightly backwards; and with another cautery in the middle of the chest, and another above the stomach. And with three cauteries from behind: one in that which is between the two shoulder blades; and with two cauteries from the two sides of the chest, below the cautery which is between the two shoulder blades.
And you should not press your hand with the cautery, rather it should be in plain view, smelling the skin.
And some ancient ones have said that there are people who use a cautery made of iron, similar to a rod; and they burn, and they insert it into that which is between the ribs, until they reach the abscess itself, and pus comes out; just as we have said in the abscess of the liver.
But in this perforation with a cautery there is fear that either the weak person dies immediately, or a fistula occurs in the place, which has no cure.
Of the method of cauterizing the spleen, Chapter XXXII.
When you treat the illness of the spleen, with what we have said concerning treatment in the division of illnesses, and your treatment does not help, then the cautery is used on it in three ways, all of which are correct.
One of which is to make three cauteries, or four, by drawing lines along the length of the spleen, according to the shape of the liver cauteries, whose shape preceded.
And let there be between each cautery a quantity equal to the thickness of a finger, or a little more or less.
And let the method of the cautery be, as we said in the cautery of the liver, equally.
And do not press your hand with the cautery; and let the sick person lie weakly on his back.
And another method of cauterization is: that you heat the cautery having two prongs, which we mentioned in the chapter on the dislocation of the shoulder; and raise the skin, which is directly over the spleen, where the left elbow of the sick person reaches; and let your raising of the skin be according to the width of the body, so that the cauteries fall along the length of the body.
Then introduce the two very hot prongs until, with them, you penetrate the skin on the other side; then withdraw the cautery; therefore four cauteries are made.
And if you wish to cauterize with another cautery having three prongs.
Then treat the cautery after you let it emit pus for many days; for it is more beneficial than any of the previous treatments.
Of the method of cauterization in dropsy.
The cautery does not fall upon dropsy unless properly applied.
When you treat a dropsical patient with the methods of treatment that we have discussed in the division, and the treatment is not effective, then you should cauterize him with four cauteries around the navel, and one cautery above the stomach, and another cautery above the liver, and a cautery above the spleen, and two cauteries behind the back between the vertebrae, and one in the direct line of the chest, and another in the direct line of the stomach: and the depth of the cautery should be approximately the thickness of the skin.
Then leave the cautery open, so that it may emit pus for a long time.
And do not remove the infirm patient from the treatment after the cautery with him; for it is necessary that two intentions be aggregated in him; and healing will hasten to him with the help of God.
The shape of the cautery with which the belly is cauterized should be pointed, according to the shape that preceded it; and the shape of the cautery with which the back is cauterized should be olive-shaped, according to the shape that preceded it.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the Feet and Legs.
When abscesses occur in a hydrops patient, and they are filled with yellow water, it is necessary to cauterize on the back of the foot, in the nocrati, which is between the auricular and annular [areas]; and raise your hand with the cautery, and do not turn it; then raise your hand; and do not repeat it at all.
For the yellow water will sweat out, and the cautery should be of this form.
Then make two cauteries on each leg, and let the cautery be made with the knife-like extremity of the cautery; and let the cautery be made along the length of the leg, one below the knee, and the other below that, approximately in the middle of the leg; and on each thigh, make two cauteries; and leave the cautery open without treatment for a long time, so that some water may sweat from it; then treat it with the rest of what we have said.
Concerning the method of cauterization in abdominal distension.
Chapter XXXV.
When abdominal distension is due to cold and dampness, weakening the retentive and digestive powers in the stomach and intestines; and it is treated with methods of healing, but is not cured; and you see the patient tolerating a cautery of exuberant strength, then cauterize him with a large cautery on his stomach, according to what preceded in the cauterization of the stomach with a circular cautery, and four subtle cauteries around the navel, with a subtle spatula-like cautery; and a large cautery, or two cauteries, above the alcatin, above the alhosos.
And if you see excessive moisture, and the patient tolerates it, then cauterize him with a cautery on the breastbone, and a cautery on each hip; and perhaps add two small cauteries near the large one on the stomach.
For it is a beneficial treatment, whose aid does not err.
Concerning the method of cauterizing Hemorrhoids.
Chapter XXXVI.
When in the anus there are many old hemorrhoids, or one, and they are from thick, cold humors, or corrupted moisture, and they are treated with what we said in the division, and the treatment does not help: then cauterize with three cauteries on the lower spine of the back under the [or: by] the almeidati for a little while triangularly, and with a cautery under the navel by almost two fingers' width.
And if you think that his stomach is chilled, and his food is not digested, and you see his face becoming ulcerated, then cauterize him on the stomach with a large cautery, as was previously described; and cauterize him on his liver, and another on his spleen, with a sharp cautery; and leave the cautery open for a time; then treat him until he is healed.
Chapter XXXVII.
When you excise althelul, then heat the cautery that resembles a ray. Then introduce the heated cautery into the excised althelul: and with your hand, until the cautery reaches the opening of the vein, from which the blood flows: do this once, or twice.
If therefore the althelul are many, then cauterize each one with the cautery as we have described. Then treat them with what you apply of ointments, until they heal.
And if you cauterize it with a large cautery over the alcatin, it is more helpful.
Concerning the method of cauterizing a fistula in the anus.
Chapter Thirty-Eight.
When the sick person does not obey the incision and the work which we have described in its place, and is frightened by it, perhaps he is cured with a cautery.
Therefore, when a fistula occurs to someone, and becomes old, pus runs from it, and corrupted humors. Therefore, it is fitting that you probe it with a fine probe. Then ascertain the amount of its depth with the probe.
Then heat the cautery, which is similar to a ray. Then insert yourself the heated cautery into the fistula itself, and the amount in which the cautery entered.
And apply the cautery repeatedly to it, until all those corrupt bodies are burned, once, or twice, or thrice, according to your need.
And guard yourself from burning any nerve, if there be any there, or large vein; or if the fistula leads to the bladder, or to the body of the intestine, then guard yourself from all these places.
And do not do this, unless when the fistula is in a fleshy place; and you think, because it is not penetrating.
Then treat the place until it is healed.
If, however, the place is sealed, and the materials are cut away from it, and it remains like this for a long time, then know that it is now completely healed.
And if they do not cut away materials from it, then know that it is penetrating, or a corrupt bone is within its depth, or something similar to those things: whose description will come in its proper place.
On the method of cauterizing the Kidneys.
When pain in the kidneys occurs from cold or from heavy winds, and it diminishes because of the weakness of the sufferer, then it is necessary to cauterize it on the almethen, over the kidneys, cauterizing over each kidney with a clauili cautery, whose description preceded.
And perhaps we cauterize it a second time on the same almeidatu. Therefore, three lines will result. Therefore, the last will be more helpful.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the bladder.
When weakness and softening of the bladder occur due to cold and moisture, to the point that the patient cannot retain urine, then cauterize it on the lower part of the summit above the bladder, where the hairs of the pubic area begin.  Cauterize with one cautery from the right side of the summit, and another from the left: and let the length of each cautery be according to the size of a thumb's breadth.  And cauterize it with a cautery from the lower back, or with two cauteries if that one is insufficient. And let it be in accordance with the previous cautery closure.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the womb.
When cold and moisture occur in the womb, and it is thereby prevented from conception, and her menstrual flow is corrupted, and its expulsion is delayed, and pain occurs to her at their arrival, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with three cauteries in a circle around the navel, as we said in the cauterization of the bladder, and with a cautery above the hip, or with two cauteries below the back: and let the cautery be a closing cautery.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the anus in dislocation.
When mucous humors discharge into the anus, and become the cause of its exit from its place, and the sign of this is that the leg is extended over the other when they are compared to each other, and the place of the dislocation is found empty there.
Therefore, it is necessary that you cauterize the affected area above the anus itself with a cautery in a similar circle, after you have marked it with ink around the anus as it revolves, and that the anus itself falls in the middle of the circle.
If this cautery is not available to you, then cauterize it with three cauteries, using a large olive-shaped cautery, and let the cautery depth correspond to the thickness of the entire skin.
Then treat it until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in Sciatica.
When pain occurs in the hip joint, and its cause is cold and dampness; and the patient is treated as we described in the division, and the treatment does not help, and it becomes longstanding; then it is necessary to free the patient from thick humors with foul pills, or with artificial pills, and similar ones. Then cauterize it.
And the method of cautery in it is according to two ways: either cautery with burning medicines, or cautery with fire.
Cautery with fire, is according to many ways.
One of which is to cauterize over the hip joint itself with three triangular cauteries, according to this shape. And make them a good or bad depth. And let the space that is between each cautery be the thickness of a finger: and let the cautery be olive-shaped.
Sometimes however, the cautery is made in the middle over the head of the hip itself. Therefore there are four cauteries.
And if you wish to cauterize with a circle, whose form preceded in the cauterization of the dislocation of the hip, one: so that the circle encompasses the entire hip.
And burn the thickness of the entire skin.
This is the method of cautery in sciatica, when the pain is adhering to the hip itself, and does not extend to the thigh and leg.
However, if it extends to the thigh and leg, then cauterize it with two cauteries on the thigh, over the place to which the sufferer there points, where the pain is, and with your cautery on the calf four fingers to the wild side for a little while: and let the cautery be a cutting one.
And let the depth of the cautery be according to the depth of the thickness of the skin.
If the patient indicates that the pain extends almost to the toes, then cauterize it there where he indicates with a puncturing cautery, three, or four, or more, if it needs it.
And if he indicates the pain to be below the knee towards the leg, then cauterize it there with one cutting cautery.
And beware in all your cauterizations, that you do not proceed with the cautery to the point of burning a nerve, or a large artery, and drawing thereby upon the patient a bad harm or contraction.
And indeed I have seen one or another, of those who have cauterized above the ankle, and have proceeded too far in the cauterization, and the leg has become swollen, until a tumor reached the foot, and the entire foot has been perforated and corrupted: then the belly's dissolution has occurred, and death after it.
If the pain is in two parts simultaneously, cauterize each according to this method.
And certain wise men have said concerning the cauterization of the buttock, of which this is the mode of cautery. Make a similar cautery of iron, whose diameter be half a palm: and let it be at its opening according to the thickness of a date-stone, or a little less: and within that cautery let there be a third cautery.
And let the space that is between each cautery be the amount of a thumb's knot: and let the cauteries be open on both sides: and let their height be like one knot, or two knots: and make for them a handle of iron fitting well into the cauteries.
Then let it be heated in the fire until it glows red and throws off sparks; then let it be placed upon the wound of the buttock of the sick person lying on his healthy side. Therefore cauterize him with three round cauteries in one turn.
Then let him be left alone for three days. Afterwards apply a plaster with butter; and leave the wound open for many days. Then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Albucasis says, "By this kind of cautery, my children, we have used little, because of the terror of its appearance; and because we have found few who will await over it.
However, it is among the good cauteries for him who endures it and finds its place with him.
A cautery, however, is with burning medicines, so that you make two samia having a perforated armilla, into which the hinge of its gate descends, of bronze or iron, the length of the wall; of which in their height there shall be two knots, or as if themselves.
And let the space that is between both quantities be the thickness of a finger, and let them be open below and above; and let that which contains them to each other be according to this form.
Then place it upon a box of ashes, the sick person lying on the healthy side. And press your hand heavily upon the box of ashes. Then pour between the two circles some warm water, which has been heated a little while with fire, and hold it for the amount of an hour's time; and let the sick person tolerate its scorching and burning, for he finds the scorching as if fire, until the scorching subsides.
Then lift your hand with the instrument, and wash off the warm water from the entire ash with sweet water; then leave it for three days.
And place butter over it until the blackness of the burning is removed; and leave it for a few days, and pus will run from it. For it is the last in the aid.
Then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
If the pain extends to the hip or leg, make a poultice on it containing water, according to what you did for the ash equally.
And this is the method of hot water; and I have already written it in the treatise on the rectification of medicines. Take alkali and quicklime, each one part: grind both, and place them in a new pot, whose bottom has a small hole, according to the amount that the radius will enter; and place another glass pot under the bottom of the first pot; and pour over the alkali and lime from sweet water, so that both are submerged by a finger; after which, you press them with your hand with a good pressure; and leave the pot until the sharp water descends into the lower part of the glass pot.
Then collect all that water, and pour it over other lime; and strain it until it is renewed.
For it will then be very strong and sharp, which is administered in many medical operations, and in the cauterization of other members. Because it produces the operation of fire itself.
And among medicines, with which anchas are cauterized, are also things like tesisie, and honey of anacard, and lime with soap, so that both are mixed together.
And Galen, indeed, narrating, recounted the cure of a certain man from antiquity, by which the pain of the anca and the sciatic vein was cured: and he greatly magnified its efficacy. And he said, that he did not need any other treatment, and that he was healed in a single instance, until he recounted that, perhaps, he had entered a bath borne and emerged from it already healthy.
And it is to be taken from green seitaragi: and if green is not found, let dry, fresh one be taken: and it should be well rubbed with some fat, and placed over the anca, where there is pain, or the leg, or the thigh: and it should be bound and left for three hours, or for as long as the sick person feels relief from the burning. Then put him into a bath.
When, therefore, his body becomes damp, put him on a bed. For the pain recedes, and he is healed.
And know that one ought not to use a cautery with these medicines, unless after the evacuation of the body.
And Dioscorides, who said that the dung of goats, when a sciatic vein is cauterized with it, helps it: and the cautery is done in this way. Take wool, and soak it in old oil, and place it on the deep place, which is between the big toe and the heel, and is closer to the heel.
Then take the dry dung of goats, and inflame it in fire, until it becomes charcoal.
Then place it on the wool, and leave it until it is extinguished. Then do it again. Therefore do not cease to do this, until the feeling reaches the top through the middle to the ankle, and the pain ceases.
And this method of cautery is called cautery Vaccinum.
Concerning the cauterization of back pain.
Sometimes pain in the back occurs from many causes, either from an accident or a blow or an evacuation of excess, and similar things, from the infusion of cold and damp material; and cautery indeed does not apply, except in this sole species, which occurs from the infusion of cold material.
Therefore, after the patient's evacuation with foul pills, and similar things, let three lines be made on the back, where the pain is, according to the width of the affected area itself; after marking with ink five cauteries in each line, or more according to the amount that the patient's tolerance permits, and let the cauterization be done with a cautery-point.
And if you wish, cauterize with three or four cauteries with a medial cautery iron, according to this form.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in the beginning of a humpback.
This illness often happens to very young children.
And the sign of its beginning in children is: that a constriction occurs in their breathing upon raising, and movement; and you find, at the end of the dorsal spine and its vertebrae, that it has already begun to protrude above the other vertebrae.
Therefore, when you see this, and wish to treat it, then cauterize it with a cautery that is circular in this shape.
And let the cautery encompass the entire vertebral part equally; and if you wish to cauterize the circumference of the vertebra with a pointed cautery, make two or three lines, and let the points be close together.
Then treat the place, until it is healed with what we have said.
And beware, lest you apply the cautery to the hump that is formed in the spasm of the nerve.
Concerning the method of cauterization in gout, and pains in the joints.
When pains in the joints are from cold humors that are shed to any limb of the body, then when pains occur in the feet, it is customary for physicians to call it gout properly.
Therefore, when gout of a cold cause is treated with methods of cure, and the pains are not removed, then the cautery removes them.
And it is that one should cauterize it after evacuation, in the circumference of the joints of the feet, with many cauteries; and let the cautery be olive-shaped.
And if you need to puncture on the surface of the foot, then do it with a pointed cautery. If the pains ascend to the knees, or other joints, and that often happens, then cauterize it on each knee with three or four cauteries on every side, with this same claw-shaped cautery.
If, however, more cauterizations with this cautery are needed, then cauterize it. And do not immerse your hand with the cautery, rather let it be about the thickness of the skin only.
If, however, the pains ascend to the knees and back, then administer what we have said about cautery in its chapter.
If the pains are only in the hands, then prick the points around the foci, like two lines revolving.
If, however, pain remains in the fingers, then prick them, over each knot a prick, and over the palm of the hand.
If, however, the pains ascend after days to the elbows, or to the shoulders, then cauterize both from every side.
And do not evacuate the sick person from a good regimen, from the taking of medicines. For if a good regimen is made, and phlegm is evacuated, it will be healed with the help of God with this cautery.
Concerning the manner of cauterization in Ruptures.
When a rupture occurs in the groin, and the intestine, or the viscera, descend to the testicle, and it is a beginning proximate one: then it is necessary that you order the sick person to let go of eating on his day. And let him use laxatives, so that the stool descends from his belly.
Then let him sit between your hands on his back: and order him to hold his breath, until it emerges, or the viscera, or intestine, appears.
Then reduce it with your fingers, and mark with ink under the rupture, above the pubic bone, with a mark whose extremity is similar to half a circle towards the upper part of the body.
Then cauterize with a cautery, of which this is the form, until it becomes white, and throws off sparks. Then reduce the intestine, or viscus, to its concavity. Then let the attendant place his hand over the location, so that the intestine does not exit: and you now have opened between the legs of the sick person, and placed a cushion beneath him, and another attendant on his legs, and another on his chest, who holds his hands.
Then place the cautery upon that mark, with your hand holding the cautery upright. And hold it until you reach the mouth with it; or repeat with it another time, if you have not reached the mouth with it on the first attempt.
And prudently observe the exit of the intestine during your cauterization, lest you burn it, and cause death or great harm to the sick person through it.
And know that when you do not reach the mouth with the cautery, your operation is not effective.
And the cautery for infants should be fine, according to their size.
Then treat with the remaining ointments until it is healed.
And let the sick person lie on their back for forty days, until the wound is sealed.
And it is necessary that you provide nourishment for the duration of his treatment, that which will soothe his belly, so that his intestines do not exit during straining and expulsion.
Then, when he wishes to rise after forty days, then administer a properly made bandage, and let him keep it on for another forty days.
And lessen labor, and fullness of food and drink, and loud voices.
For when he uses this regimen, thus he is healed with complete healing.
And I will speak of the treatment of Ruptures with incision in his chapter.
However, when Ruptures occur in the remaining belly, and are incipient, and the force is such that they should not be added to, then cauterize the Rupture with a round cautery according to its size: and let that which is burned be from then on as its third part. Then treat him with what we have said: and it will not be added to.
And some of the first have already said that the Rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cautery, according to this shape.
After it is marked with ink, and a line is placed which is across the width on the upper side of the Rupture, and another line at the lower. And place your hand in the middle with the cautery forceps.
But the first cautery is easier and better.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in pains due to a fall or a blow.
Chapter XLVIII.
When pain occurs in certain limbs from a fall or blow, and that pain persists for a long time, and treatment with medicines does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize with a pointed cautery.
And let the cautery of each limb be a cautery according to its size, and its smallness, and its weakness, and its strength, and the location of the twisting, and the pain from it.
If therefore it is healed from the first cautery, it is well. If not, then repeat the cautery upon it.
Because it is customary for these pains to shift from one limb to another that is near it. Therefore it is necessary to pursue them with cautery until the infirmity is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in Leprosy.
Leprous people are sometimes greatly helped by cauterization. And especially the type of leprosy that occurs due to the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy: therefore, when you intend to cauterize it, consider this.
If the leprosy is spreading, and you have treated it with what we have stated in the division, and it does not descend nor remain stationary; and you fear that the corruption will spread to the entire constitution of the sick person, then cauterize him on the head with five cauteries: one in the middle of the head's mark, and a second below it toward the forehead at the end of the hair, and two above the two horns, and one behind above the base of the neck.
And with your cautery, hold your hand a little while, until a small impression is made on the bone, and the cortices are loosened from it: so that the expulsion of coarse vapors from it may be relieved, and cauterize also with the cautery on the spleen itself, according to what has preceded.
However, if the leprosy has already spread over the sick person, and is clearly visible, then it is necessary to cauterize with those cauteries that we have mentioned for the head, and with a cautery on the tip of the nose, and with two cauteries on the two cheekbones, and with two cauteries on the vertebrae of the neck, and with six on the vertebrae of the back, and with one large one on the haunches near the tail, and one on the haunch itself, in the haunch itself; and with two on the hips; namely, one on each hip, and two on the knees; one on each knee, and two on the shoulders, and two on the elbows, and two on the soft parts of his chest; and cauterize him on every joint, from the joints of his fingers of the hands and feet; and cauterize on every heel of his feet, and the joints of his hands.
And beware of the nerves that are above the heel's last part, so that you do not burn them.
And sometimes a cautery is applied to the breastbone, and another to the stomach bone, and another to the liver.
And know that the more you apply the cautery, the more help it is and the more beneficial it is.
And know that the sick person does not find pain in the cautery, as healthy people find it, because his body is already numbed.
And the cauteries should be of varying sizes, large and small, according to the limbs and joints, according to what has been previously stated regarding the types of instruments.
Then treat the cautery with herb flour and honey, and with the rest of the treatment, until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing in a state of stupor.
When any limb is numb and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and is not healed, then cauterize that numb limb with cauteries, according to the size of the limb, whether large or small.
And let your cautery enter the thickness of the skin a little. Then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
And sometimes it is cauterized for a numbness that happens to the hand and foot, in the spinal column of the back at the exit points of the nerves that move that limb, and the numbness is removed.
But let no one presume upon it unless he is knowledgeable in the anatomy of the limbs and the exit points of the nerves that move the body.
Chapter LI.
When Albaras is old and no medicinal remedy helps it, then cauterize over it with a deep cautery for a short time, according to the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed and its color is changed.
Then treat it with flour of herbs, and lentils with rose oil, and arnogloss leaves, and pigeon's blood, and swallow's blood: let each be one part: mix these all, and spread them over a cloth, and apply to the area until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in Cancer.
When Cancer is incipient and you wish to stop it, then cauterize it with a circular cautery around it, just as it revolves.
However, the wise said that it should be cauterized with the final cautery in the middle.
However, it does not seem to me, for I fear that it will ulcerate; and I have already seen it do so on several occasions.
And it is better that it be cauterized in a circle around it, as we said, or with many cauteries.
Concerning the manner of cauterizing in Adubelati.
When someone has an Adubelati, and it is delayed in maturing, whether due to excess that causes it, or due to the age of the infirm person, when they are decrepit with little blood, or due to time, and the need to hasten the maturation of the Adubelati, then cauterize in a circle around it with many small cauteries by puncturing. Then leave it. For it will hasten with maturation.
If however you want to perforate it with a cautery, then heat the cautery, of which this is the form.
And place it in the middle of the Adubelati until it penetrates the skin; and let the cautery be from that which follows the infirm person, so that the course of the purulent matter is alleviated.
Then treat it until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing a corroding evil.
Chapter LIII.
A corroding thing is nothing but a corruption that walks in a member, and corrodes it; just as fire consumes dry wood.
If therefore you see a corroding thing in a place that can tolerate a cauterization with fire, then cauterize it with many fires, with small and large cautery irons, according to what suits the place where the corroding thing is.
Then cauterize it from every side until you uproot the entire corruption, and nothing of it remains at all.
Then leave it for three days, and put powdered sulfur mixed with oil on the cauterized areas, until all scabs and all corruption are eradicated.
Then treat it with ointments that generate flesh.
If therefore you see that after three days healthy flesh is born, in which there is no corruption, it is good.
And if not, then again cauterize that which remained of the corrupted areas.
And it is sometimes cured by corrosive medicine. For it rises in place of the cautery.
However, cautery with fire is of quicker help; and I indeed have already said that its cauterization with corrosive medicine is in division; therefore take it there when you need it.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in warts and corns.
Chapter LV.
This ailment frequently occurs in the lower parts of the feet, and it is a thick, filtered substance that harms the foot.
And cautery in them is indeed in two ways: cautery with fire, and cautery with hot water.
As for cautery with fire, make a concave cautery like a bird of prey's wing, which is made of iron, according to the size of the wart to encompass it completely, and with thin edges.
Then place it, heated, upon the wart. Then revolve the hand with the cautery in a circular motion around the wart until the cautery reaches the depth of the wart, and leave it for three days until it begins to emit pus. Then plaster it with crushed wild herbs and salt, and leave the plaster on it overnight. For it will be eradicated from its roots.
Then treat the area with a flesh-generating ointment until it heals.
If they are not cured, and often occur on the surface of the body, especially on the hands and feet, then apply a cautery to them with hot water.
